to the Sisters of Dominic of San Leandro.
Daniel McCarthy petitions for letters of
administration.
KILLED WHILE ON DUTY.
Watchman Collins Found Dead Un-
der a Railroad Car.
OAKLAND, May 4.â John Collins, an
aged watchman at the railroad yards, was
found dead under a car at daylight this
morning. A train had passed over his
chest during the night while the watch
man was crossing the track for the pur
pose of attending to one of the watch
men's clocks. Collins had been in the em
ploy of the Southern Pacific through a
generation, and when increasing age
brought with it Infirmity he was given the
position of night watchman. His duties
required him to wind up certain watch
men's clocks at different points in the
yard for the purpose of showing that he
had made his rounds at the proper time.
To reach these clocks it was necessary
sometimes to walk around a long string
of cars or else climb over them or dodge
under the drawheads. It is supposed that
he was doing this when he was run over,
having probably mistaken some cars at
tached to a locomotive for some that were
sidetracked.
The deceased was missed, and near 9
track was seen a lighted lantern. An in
vestigation showed that it belonged to
Collins, and its (had owner was found a
minute later. Collins leaves a widow and
six children.

Board of Health Out of Business.
ALAMEDA. May A.â Alameda Is with
out a Board of Health. The offices of the
old members were declared vacant by the
City Trustees a week ago, and the doc
tors composing the board were immedi
ately reappointed. Three of themâ Dr. G.
P. Reynolds, Dr. C. George Bull and 'Dr.
1.. VV. Stidham- resigned last night, leav
ing the board with but two members,
which is not a sufficient number to do
business. The City Trustees failed to
fill the vacancies, consequently the
Health Department of the city has vir
tually gone out of business for the time
being. The employes have no one to di
rect their movements and nobody author
ized to draw their salary warrants.
Death of A. V. Henko.
ALAMEDA, May 4.â A. V. Henko died
this afternoon at his home, ..'ill Clinton
avenue. He had been ailing for a long
time from an affection of the brain, which
produced paralysis. About two months
ago he was taken to the German Hospital
to undergo a surgical operation, but the
physicians stated his case was hopeless
and that in- would die within a month.
Later he was treated at Fabiola Hospital,
Oakland, and returned home a few weeks
ago apparently somewhat Improved in
health. Deceased was a native of Rus
sia, aged 39 years. He leaves a widow
and three children. His remains will bt.
cremated.

NOTICE is hereby given by order of the Board
of Directors of the OCEANIC STEAMSHIP
COMPANY' that a meeting of the stockholders
of said Company has been called by said
Board, to be held on FRIDAY, the second day
of .Tune, A. D. 1899, at eleven o'clock In the
forenoon of said day, at the principal place of
business of said Company, at the building
where the said Board of Directors usually
meets, namely, at the office of said Company,
number 227 Market st., in the City and County
of San Francisco, State of California; that
the object of said meeting Is to consider and
act upon the proposition that said Company
create a bonded Indebtedness of two million
five hundred thousand dollars (12,500,000 00), In
United States gold coin, for the purpose of
raising money to complete the construction
' of Its steamships and their equipment, for
use In the business of this corporation, and
to purchase and pay for any other property
within the purposes of this Company; and to
secure the bonded indebtedness so proposed
to be created by a mortgage upon Its steam
and sailing ships and all other property of
said Company now owned or hereafter to be
acquired by said Company.
By order of -the Board of Directors of the
Oceanic Steamship Company.

~ NOTICE.
To All Whom It May Concernâ Notice is
hereby given that on the 17th day of April
1899, the Bakersfield and Los Angeles Rail-
way Company filed Its application In writing
in the office of the Clerk of the Superior
Court of the City and County of San Fran-
cisco, addressed to the Superior Court of said
county, making application for the voluntary
dissolution of the Bakersfield and Los An-
geles Railway Company, which said petition
and application stated that at a meeting of
the stockholders of said company on the 13th
day of April, 1899, called for the purpose of
passing upon the questlcn, It was resolved to
have a voluntary dissolution of the corpora-
tion, and that such resolution was passed by
a two-thirds vote of all the stockholders and
that all the claims and demands against the
corporation, of every kind, nature and descrip-
tion, have been fully paid and discharged
Wherefore, it was ordered by the said Su-
perior Court upon the filing of said petition
i and application that the undersigned, as
â¢ Clerk of said Court, give a notice of such ap-
I plication by publication In some newspaper
published In the City and County of San
I Francisco, for a period of thirty-five days
Therefore, all persons having any interest In
I the matter of said application or desiring to
oppose the granting of the same are here-
; by notified to file in my office, on or before
the 22d day of May, 1899. any and all objec-
j tions which they may have to the granting of
said petition.
In testimony whereof, I have hereunto set my
! hand and the official seal of said court this
the 17th day of April. 189?.
(Seal). WILLIAM A. DEANE.
County Clerk and ex-Offlcio Clerk of the
Superior Court.
By E. M. THOMPSON,
Deputy County Clerk and ex-Offlcio Deputy
Clerk of the Superior Court.

Strange Fate of Mary
Jackson.

PLUNGED FROM THIRD FLOOR
â¦ â
THE IDEA OF SUICIDE NOT CON

-! â â â¦
The Victim Was a Sleepwalker and
Had Suffered for Many Years
From Nervous Dis
orders.
â¦â
'
Miss Mary Jack! either fell or
jumped out of a third-story window in
the La Mar boarding hoi:- on the north
oast corner of Bush and Stockton streets,
early yesterday morning and sustained
Injuries which the doctors say will prove
fatal.
At about 1 o'clock Policeman Charles
Fennell, who was patrolling his beat, dis
covered the senseless form â >; a woman
dressed in her nightclothes lying on the
sidewalk in front of the house, and on
further investigation saw blood flowing
from a wound in the head. The body
was at once removed to the apartment
where her mother, who was her constant
attendant' was still ping. Dr. Mc-
Swain. who rooms in the house, was
called and found the skull badly frac
tured, besides a compound fracture of
the right hip.
The relatives scout the Idea of at
tempted suicide. They ascribe the acci
dent to the young woman's somnambulis
tic habit, and the delirium resulting from
over three years of ill health. She was
very sick on Wednesday evening and re
titr'ed at 1 o'clock.
It is supposed that she noiselessly left
The side or her sleeping mother, opened
the lower window, which was always
kept closed, and dropped forty feet to the
sidewalk below.
About a month ago Miss Jackson was
brought over from Berkeley by her
mother and taken to the Women's Hos
pital, where an ration was performed
for a nervous trouble with which she had
long been afflicted. She had only left the
hospital a few days ago nd though she
A SOMNAMBULIST'S FATAL FALL.
had not been suffering pain she was in
a highly excitable condition. Her nerves
were unstrung, and to this fad is as
cribed the cause of the accident. She is
28 years of age and has many relatives
in this city.
Dr. E. S. Howard, who Is now in at
tendance on the case, says that she may
die any minute. The fracture of the
thigh and pelvic bone, and the lacerated
wound of the scalp, he considers will
prove fatal.
MILITARY WEDDING
ON ANGEL ISLAND
DRUM MAJOR ARNDT MARRIED
TO MISS CLYDE KEITH.
Bride Given Away by Major Hess,
Commander of the Post, and
Chaplain Potter Performs
the Ceremony.
The soldiers on Angel Island were
treated to quite a change from the usual
routine of military life yesterday. There
was a wedding at the post and every
man in the garrison, except those on
duty, crowded the chapel to see the cere
mony performed.
The groom was Drum Major Paul Arndt
and the bride was Miss Clyde Keith of
the Presidio. The couple were made one
by Chaplain Potter of the post, and Major
Frank W. Hess, commanding officer at
Angel Island, gave the bride away. The
regimental band was in attendance and
played Mendelssohn's wedding march as
the bride and groom left the church. One
of the first to salute the newly wedded
couple was Captain Btofen of the quar
termaster's steamer McDowell. He knows
all the young people at Angel Island, Al
catraz. Lime Point, Fort Point and the
Presidio, and considers It his bounden
duty to kiss the bride at each wedding.
On this occasion he was a little late and
the groom pot the first kiss.
Drum Major' Arndt is the son of Ser
geant Otto Arndt, leader of the band.
Ie Is a universal favorite and the con
gratulations that poured in on himself
and wife were of the heartiest kind.

Unknown Drowned Man.
The body of an unknown man was
found floating in the bay at the foot of
Berry street wharf yesterday morning by
Fred Carson of 30"^ Gefieva street. There
was nothing on the person by which the
corpse could be identified. The body had
been In the water several days and was
very much decomposed. The remains are
at the Morgue awaiting identification.
WANT PROTECTION.
Property Owners on the San Bruno.
Road Petition for an Engine
House.
Property-owners and residents in the
vicinity of San Bruno road and Army
street have petitioned the Supervisors for
better protection against Are in that
neighborhood. The petition was headed
by Morris Windt, who has thousands of
dollars' worth of property at the Junc
tion of the two streets mentioned, and i
other owners of realty adjacent thereto
and also several residents further 'out on
the San Bruno road. The attention of the
Supervisors is directed to the locality as
being one thickly doited by factories in
which considerable capital is invested in
machinery and other plants, all of which
would become totally destroyed in case
of a large fire breaking out in any one
of the numerous factories. To afford pro
tection against such a contingency the
city fathers are requested to provide an
appropriation for the construction of an
engine-house in the locality mentioned,
and in addition to this to notify the
Spring Valley Water Company to lay B
inch mains In place of the 4-inch ones now
In use then . as in case of fire the supply
would be entirely Inadequatae to meet the
necessity of the case.
At the present time the nearest engine
house to this place is located on Folsom
street, between Twenty-first and Twenty
second, and the time consumed in reach
ing San Bruno road in answering an
alarm would be so long that the place
attacked by lire would be beyond relief
by th. time the apparatus would reach
there.
IMPROVEMENT IN THE
CITY'S NORTH END
PLAN TO WIDEN WASHINGTON
STREET FIVE BLOCKS.
Many Property Owners Favor the
Move, but Much Must Be Done
First Question of Cost.
The proposition to widen Washington
street from Montgomery avenue to the
water front was discussed yesterday at
a public meeting called by the executive
committee of the North Central Improve
ment Association. H. P. Sonntag, the
president, in opening the meeting stated
that it is the expressed wish of quite a
number of the larger property owners in
that section of the city to have tha im
provement made by taking about twenty
five feet from the south side of the street,
so as to conform to the width of Mont
gomery avenue. It is advisable to obtain
the opinion of the majority of property
owners first, as the association is not
ready to endorse such a movement until
it could see what the outcome would be.
1.. V. Merle, representing the Montgom
ery estate on Washington street and
Montgomery avenue, stated that the old
block bearing the name of the first owner
is about to be renovated an'! repaired in a
modern style. If th.- street is to, be wid
ened be wanted to know it so as to make :
allowances for the loss of the north end.
Personally he was in favor of the im
provement and the estate was willing to
stand its share â¢'â¢' the expense. He knew
that many of the larger owners, not pres
ent, were also In favor of the change,
while those living at the farther end of
the avenue indorsed the move to a man.
Supervisor Holland stated that the Board
of Supervisors are willing to improve the
city and would certainly make arrange
ments tÂ«. carry out any plans that the ,
people of the district would advise.
George D. Shadburne ami several oth
ers suggested that it would be a very
good idea to ascertain the cost of the
proposed change, now many would be af
fected and the exact number for and
against the plan, tie stated that he had
upon good authority that the Supervisors
had decided to grant the franchise for the
corkscrew street-car line that the rail
road people want to run into the district.
Among others who were present and
spoke were William Giselman. Hugh Hud
dleson. G. H. Berton. K. R. Provines, Ed
gar Painter. George K. Fitch, R. D.
Chandler and others. No action was
taken in toe matter, the desire being to
secure information before proceeding as
to the cost of the widening and the means
of proceeding.
CARVED HIS DEBTORS.
â  â  ._.
Sing Lee Quong Stabbed Two Chinese
Undertakers Because They Would
Not Pay What They Owed.
Lung Hing and Tong Bun Sayou, un
-1 dertakers at 724 Pacific street, were
stabbed and slashed severely yesterday
forenoon by Sing Lee Quong. They had
had a dispute about money matters, and
Quong attacked them with a Chinese
machete, lacerating the muscles of the
scalp and shoulders. The wounded men
were treated at the Harbor Hospital and
the murderous assailant was placed un
der arrest by Officer Peshon.
The prisoner denies that he inflicted the
wounds. He said that he was upstairs
asleep in his room when the trouble be
gan and that he ran downstairs as an un
known Chinaman was slashing the under
takers. Quong said also that he was a
cook and that the wounded men owed
him money and would not pay him. al
though he had nothing to eat. He gavo
his age as 62 years.
Last night Sing Lee Quong told the po
lice officers that about two months ago
he had seen Ton Bun Sayou bury a child
In a vacant lot on the corner of Pacific
and Stockton streets. He was sent out in
company with two officers and after a
few minutes' digging the body was un
earthed. It was of a male Chinese child
apparently about a month old, and in an
advanced state of decomposition. Sing
Lee Quong claims he does not know who
the child's parents were.
POKER PLAYERS IN COU_.IT.
Getting a Jury in the Case of W.
Redman of the Palace Saloon.
The first of the cases of the poker
players arrested during the police raid
last week to be tried by a jury was called
in Judge Graham's court yesterday after
noon. It was that of W. Redman, charged
with carrying on a percentage game in
the Palace saloon, 887 Market street.
A venire of 100 had been issued but
when the court adjourned at 5 o'clock
only two out of thirty examined had been
accepted. They were John Utschlg and
Charles Fredericks. Four of the Jurors
sent substitutes and at the request of
Chief Lees the Judge issued attachments
for their appearance in court when the
case la called this afternoon. They were
A. H. Brod, N. C. Llndsley, T. McCarthy
and J. O. Dwyer. Prosecuting Attorney
Wentworth has exhausted all of his per
emptory challenges.
Knew the Combination.
William Springer, a coal dealer at 400
Dolores street, swore to a complaint in
acting Judge Groezinger's court yester
day charging James Fagan with grand
larceny. Fagan formerly worked for him
and knew the combination of the safe,
and he alleges that Fagan on April 28
opened the safe and stole $51 S3.

â¦
Closing Banquet of the Unitarian
Conference Enlivened by Some
Strong Talk About Modern

The close of the Unitarian conference,
which has been In session In Oakland
SUCCESSOR, TO MISS BLOCH.
+ .New Secretary to the Golden Sate
$ Park, Commissioners.
.MISS JODGE FJIIIUUWI.
Â© â¢â /riSS MADGE FAIRMAN, a popular young lady of this city, has been -
_ IVI named thÂ« successor to Miss Valence V. Bloch as secretary to the Board (
â¦ 111 of Golden Gate Park Commissioners. Miss Fairman is well fitted for the -
O position and will soon assume her duties. She has numerous friends <
4- and all of them rejoice at her appointment. Her education was obtained *
*â¢*-* in this State and her general knowledge will greatly assist the board in
X wrestling -with many troublesome problems pertinent to the city's large ,
+ pleasure ground.
?Â©*Â©+ O^O-f Â©â¦Â©4 Â©â¦ O â¦ Â©+Â©+Â©+Â© +Â©+Â©+Â©+Â©+ Â©4Â©â¦ Â©â¦Â© â¦Â©â¦Â©â¦Â©+â¢
for the past few days, was fittingly cele
brated by a banquet extended by the Uni
tarian Club of California at the Mer
chants' Club last evening. About 400 were
seated in the dining room, which was
profusely adorned with floral decorations.
Toasts, interspersed with selections by
the Press Club Quartet, were responded
to by Rev. Btopford W. Brooke, Rev.
C. J. K. Jones of Los Angeles, Chaplain
F. C. Brown, l". S. N., and Hon. John P.
Irish. Rev. Dr. Brooke touched upon,
"The Present Function of Unitarlanism,"
and Rev. Dr. Jones spoke of "The Power
of the Unitarian Pulpit." Both of the
clergymen were warmly applauded and
made the most of the subjects they han
dled.
Chaplain F. C. Brown of the battleship
lowa was heartily received when he arose
Jto speak. The subject allotted to him
| was "Theological Co-operation," and he
i handled it in a manner somewhat sur
j prising to most of his audience. His tone
was forcible, and profound attention wits
observed throughout bis remarks. He be
gan by observing that many Christian
' people who were clamoring for the Chris
i tianizing of the black man in the Philip
pines had given little thought to the
; evils prevalent at their own doors; that
i no attention has been given to the correc
tion of the thousands of crooked human
ways, or to the great absorbing monopo
lies and trade corruptions, simply because
i they were backed by wealth and power,
I and created by men born in an en-
I lightened land. As # an example of the
first he referred to pathetic cases which
had come under his observation while in
San Francisco. "A woman," he said,
i "was sentenced. to three months in the
County Jail for vagrancy. A paper in
mentioning the case stated that she was
the woman who had caused the impris
onment of the wretch responsible for her
1 downfall, a number of years ago. At the
\ time of her first sin no helping hand had
i been outstretched to save her, and now
i it has come to pass that the only mes
sage the great city of San Francisco can
; extend to this poor wretch is three
i months behind prison bars. Such a thing
i causes the finger of scorn to be pointed
at every church in the city.
"The idea of Christianity, as it is prac
i ticed to-day, is that when a life has fallen
! from grace it should no longer find refuge
lin the sanctuary of the church. Only
i those who have the mystic symbolism
stamped upon their countenances are fit
for the consolations of religion, and the
efforts of the Gospel to spread the Spirit
of God should be confined to far-away
blacks and not to the outcasts at home.
There are preachers to-day who plight
their troth in sensational sermons, the
titles of which reflect on the purity of
sacred life. They circulate nonsensical
tracts and send them to foreign lands.
All of these things have a tendency to
keep people from church rather than
draw them to it. Practical and not un
natural methods should be employed in
tha conversion of sinners, and until this
thing is understood little advancement
will be made in the way of real reform at
home or abroad.
"The theme of my remarks is 'Theolog
ical Co-operation,' and by such co-opera
tion men of the cloth will only be enabled
to execute the work they have been com
missioned to do. Religious denominations
will closet themselves in their little shells
on Sunday discussing the particular dog
mas of their creed and denouncing some.
other denomination, while us a matter of
fact they agree with the objects of their
denunciation in nine points out of ten.
When they come together and recognize
that they are all working to attain the
same end, and that the rough road will be
traveled only by hearty co-operation, and
not by dissension, then will the great
problem be solved. Chaplains of the navy
âand we are about twenty-four in num
berâmingle with our men on week days,
giving them all the benefit of bright ex
ample, and on Sunday preach of God, of
purity and heaven, and do not herald our
words with sensational headlines calcu
lated to inspire their disgust instead of
their reverence."
Rev. Mr. Brown was followed by Hon.
John P. Irish, who spoke on the Czar's
peace congress to be opened at The
Hague on the ISth of the present month.
With his usual aggressiveness of speech
Mr. Irish denounced the present war in
the Philippines and held up the acts-com
mitted by Americans upon the wounded
of the enemy as atrocities of a barbaric
period. He read portions of communica
tions received from the soldiers and when
he came to the report of Lieutenant Du
boee on the burning of the Pace Church
said Duboce was a monster. In part he
said:
"The Czar has proposed a peace con
gress. It has been treated lightly by the
nations of the earth and I regret to
think that it will result in naught. It is
to be hoped that it may accomplish one
thing, if nothing else, and that is to re
solve some means by which the weak can
be protected against the arm of the
mighty. War is becoming more brutal
and it has got to such a state that the
amusement of civilized soldiers rests in
unmercifully crushing the uncivilized man
out of existence. There should be some
revolt at the thought that men can be
permitted to burn the wounded of the
enemy like mice in a strawstack. Let
some court be afforded to which the
weak can appeal for justice."
On the effects of the present war the
speaker said: "I think that the future
will demonstrate that, at this particular
time, war has been disastrous to this
country. It has checked the flow of
peace and good will among men. Eighteen
months ago we were at peace with all
nations, but to-day we have inspired a
fear among nations that has robbed us of
our tranquil standing. At the most, war
but arouses in our hearts the sleeping ap
petites of the serpent and the shark and
breeds the desire of conquestâ that desire
to swallow up the small in a mlghly
gulp."
Kipling's poem. the speaker denounced
as -an error. He said it was intended to
overthrow a truth which had oeen estab
lished with the dawn of Christianity and
set up a theory that a wrong la right just
because it is a burden.
"ACTORS" COME TO GRIEF.
Two Eootlight "Favorites" Arrested
for Defrauding a Hotel.
Herbert Wolf and F. â¢'.. Belmont, young
men with histrionic aspirations, were ar
rested last evening by Police Officer Syl
vester and Marshal Ramage of Hay
wards. They are charged with defraud
ing D. G. Frantz, a hotel keeper of Hay
wards, out of three days' board bill.
Accompanied by another stage-struck
friend named Waldemeyer, Wolf and Bel
mont went to I lay wards, intending to
make their debut and incidentally to re
plenish their depleted purses. After rent
ing the Town Hall the trio had a number
of hand bills printed, announcing that
they would give a show at "popular
prices."
Wolf was billed as the only rival to
the great Hermann, his "tricks of leger
demain fairly dazzling the beholder."
Evidently realizing that their maiden ef
fort would not be a success, the trio
packed their grips and skipped without
having settled with the hotel man for
board. On learning of their sudden de
parture Frantz went before the. Town
Justice and swore to complaints, charg
ing them with defrauding an innkeeper.
Wolf and Belmont were found on Mar
ket street and taken back to Haywards,
where they will be tried under the State
law, which makes it an offense to "beat"
a hotel keeper. Waldemeyer has not yet
been arrested.

Witnesses Testify That the Signa
tures on the Alleged Bogus De
mand Were Forged Ce
rtified To by Accused.
Peter W. McGlade was treated to a bit
ter disappointment yesterday morning
when Judge Cook rendered a decision over
ruling the objections of * his attorney,
Patrick Reddy, to the admission as evi
dence against him of the alleged forged
demand for street work on. which the in
dictment of the Grand Jury was based.
Ex-Street Superintendent Ambrose's for
mer bookkeeper and his attorney had
built high hopes on barring out this im
portant document and had they succeed
ed McGlade would have got off scot free
on all the charges pending against him.
As it is the evidence -will go to the jury.
In rendering his decision Judge Cook
took up the objections of defendant's
counsel one by one and disposed of them
in short order. The court held that the
contention that the document was void
on its face and therefore not a tit sub
ject for an indictment for forgery be
cause the signatures of Assistant Super
intendent of Streets 'lark and Assistant
Clerk of the Board of Supervisors Mc-
Ginnls were valueless, even if genuine,
was Insufficient ground for objection.
"The document," he said, "so far as it
travels down to the Auditor's allowance,
appears to be a demand for the payment
of money. Attached -to it is an affidavit
which purports to prove the genuineness
Of the demand. Now it Is charged that
all three signatures of Swords, Clark and
McGinnls are forged. So it comes down
to a forged document for payment with
forged evidence of its correctness. So if
the people can prove that it. is forged
â *-' far the allegations of the complaint
with regard to the making of the forgery
will have been sustained. .1.
"With regard to th.- uttering of the for
geryâfor the crime of forgery consists of
two acts, making and utteringâ the de
mand having been allowed by the Audi
tor, that portion of it containing the Au
ditor's allowance may i" open to objec
tion that no one was injured thereby. But
1. think evidence should go to the jury."
Immediately following the rendering of
the decision the introduction of evidence
going to prove the forgery and thus pav
ing the way for th.- admission of the doc
ument was begun. Hi J. Swords, in whose
name the demand was made, was re
called and swore that he had never
signed th.- paper and that he had never
worked for the Street Department. He
was followed by former Superintendent
ot Streets Ambrose, who explained the
methods in vogue In the office in regard
to' the tiling of demands and of the dis
covery of McGlade' 8 alleged crime.
Thomas .1. Clark testified thai he was
a deputy in the office "i the Superinten
dent of Streets when the bogus demand
was filed and he swore positively that he
had never affixed his signature to the '
forged document. He also testified that
while serving in the Street Department I
he had entire charge of the sewer work ;
and that Swords was never employed in
that department. - ?;-.â â 
At the afternoon session more of the
same kind of evidence was Introduced,
but not without objection on the part
of the defendant's counsel, who stub
bornly contested every point. The most
important testimony of the day was the
positive declaration of M. M. Regensbur
ger. a money broker, that the signature
of P. W. McGlade, which appears on the
back of the demand, certifying that
i .
PRINCIPAL AND SOME WITNESSES IN THE McGLAOE TRIAL.
Swords had performed work for the
Street Department in the month of
August, IS9S, for which he was entitled
to JW. was in the handwriting of the de
fendant. The witness testified that lie
was familiar with the writing of Mc-
Glade and produced a number of notes
signed by the defendant at various times
in his presence to compare with the sig
nature on the forged demand. After con
siderable sparring these were, admitted in
evidence. Regensburger is the princi
pal sufferer through the alleged forgeries j
of the defendant, as he cashed a num
ber of tags bearing McGlade's signature
as deputy superintendent of streets, cer
tifying that the bearers had performed
work for the city and the amount of com
pensation to which they were entitled, a
number of which turned out to be bogus.
Harry Piper, who was Chief Deputy
County Clerk three years ago, when Mc-
Glade was appointed to a deputyshlp in
the office of Superintendent Ambrose
was called to the stand to Identify papers
in relation to the appointment and bear
ing his file mark. Piper was troubled
with a defective memory. He could not
swear to McGlade's signature and he was
not quite sure of his own. although he
thought it looked like his writing.
T. B. McGinnls, former deputy clerk of
the Board of Supervisors, was" called to
the stand and swore that his signature
which appears on me bogus demand was
forged. He also testified as to the usual
procedure in passing upon demands com
ing from the Street Department.

"Do you know anything about this de

forged document.
"Yes. sir; -that- passed through my
hands," was the reply.
"Have you any record of.it? was the
next question.
"I have." replied the witness, and he
produced a big book and pointed out the
entry referred to. Ryan also testified
that he had delivered a batch of de
mands to McGlade personally, including
the one which forms such an important
feature of the present trial, and had the
defendant's receipt for the same. ' An
other book, containing the receipt, was
produced and both were entered as ex
hibits on the part of the peonle.
At this point Assistant District Attor
ney Black asked for an adjournment, as
one of his principal witnesses. Kytka, the
handwriting expert, was out of the city,
and as his evidence was necessary to
show that signatures of Mediums. Chirk
and Swords were not only forged, but .
that they were forged by McGlade. In
fact, Mr. Black says that Kytka will tes
tify that the entire document, with the
exception of the signatures of the Audi
tor and the members ot the Auditing
Committee of the Board of Supervisors,
was written by McGlade. Judge Cook
continued the case until Monday morning

Defrauding the Revenue.
David Green and John Morist were ar
rested Wednesday on a charge of defraud
ing the revenue by neglecting to affix rev
enue stamps to articles sold by them at
the drug store formerly kept by "Waller
Bros. A Deputy Internal Revenue Col
lector bought a bottle of wine unstamped
at the store, and Miss Ida Stanford, ste
nographer in the office of Revenue Agent
Thomas, bought a box of tooth powder,
also unstamped. The prisoners were re
leased on depositing $250 bonds each.

Yesterday's Insolvents.
Douglass Creighton of the Hotel Alex
andria, at 781 Sutter street, filed a petition
in insolvency in the United States Dis
trict Court. His liabilities are $14,502 and
his assets $10,736. of which $10,100 is repre
sented by household poods. Edward
Flanagan, iron worker, of this city, filed
a petition setting forth his liabilities at
$601. He has no assets.
